In some corporate environments with an internal network, emails are trusted by default, and verification is unnecessary. It can also be a strategy for rapid onboarding, where users are allowed to try out the platform before verifying. Email verification is a stage where lead conversion can be reduced. This article discusses this topic: https://medium.com/nick-lim-ux-portfolio/case-study-how-fixing-email-verification-issues-restored-our-100-task-success-rate-be79693c752b

Is the oauth for apple broken? I'm getting "state not found" and I've checked everything thrice, the body its coming back like: ```body: { '{"state":"q5oj...","code":"c200487a....","id_token":"eyJraWQi..."}': '' }``` EDIT: I want to share what fixed it for me was that I moved ``` app.use(express.urlencoded({ extended: true })); app.use(express.json()); ``` To after ```app.all("/api/auth/{*any}", toNodeHandler(auth));``` ```const app = express(); app.set("trust proxy", true); app.all("/api/auth/{*any}", toNodeHandler(auth)); app.use(express.urlencoded({ extended: true })); app.use(express.json()); const port = 8080;```

Does anyone know? ```ts export const dymoEmailPlugin = ({ apiKey, emailRules }: DymoEmailPluginOptions) => { const defaultRules: EmailValidatorRules = { deny: ["FRAUD", "INVALID", "NO_MX_RECORDS", "NO_REPLY_EMAIL"] as NegativeEmailRules[] }; const dymoClient = new DymoAPI({ apiKey, rules: { email: { deny: emailRules?.deny ?? defaultRules.deny } } }); return { id: "dymoEmailPlugin", hooks: { before: [ { matcher: (context: any) => context.path.startsWith("/sign-up/email"), handler: createAuthMiddleware(async (ctx: any) => { const { email } = ctx.body; if (typeof email !== "string") throw new APIError("BAD_REQUEST", { message: "Email must be a string." }); const decision = await dymoClient.isValidEmail(email); if (!decision.allow) { throw new APIError("BAD_REQUEST", { message: "Email is invalid or blocked.", reasons: decision.reasons }); } ctx.dymoEmail = decision.response as DataEmailValidationAnalysis; return { context: ctx }; }) } ] } } satisfies BetterAuthPlugin; };```

Jakob Norlin
2025-09-29T09:03:55.819000+00:00
Two issues with the SSO plugin: - Users can still register with a different auth method than SSO when their domain is configured, and when they do the don't get added to the organization by default. Two possible solutions: - Disable signing up with other methods for SSO configured domains - Add the ability to add them to the SSO organization anyway if the domain matches - The SSO config is tied to user with cascade on delete, so If I set up SSO for my org, then hand over ownership to someone else and delete my account, the SSO config is deleted

2025-09-26T19:30:27.831000+00:00
why is it recommended to use the api object when integrating better-auth with next.js? RSC and Server actions The api object exported from the auth instance contains all the actions that you can perform on the server. Every endpoint made inside Better Auth is as invocable as a function. Including plugins endpoints. while when it comes to tanstack start, it is recommended to use the client SDK? TanStack Start integration: Usage tips We recommend using the client SDK or authClient to handle authentication, rather than server actions with auth.api.

Click the link to verify your email: ${url}.`, react: <VerifyEmail user={user} url={url} />, }); }, sendOnSignUp: true, // Sent email when a user signs up. sendOnSignIn: false, autoSignInAfterVerification: true, // Signs in user after verifying email. expiresIn: 60 * 60 // 1 hour for security (60 times 60 seconds = 1 hour) }, ``` I've got sendOnSignIn disabled, but when a user is unverified and tries logging in, it still sents an email. I assume this is possibly because ``` requireEmailVerification: true, // Enable email verification ``` However I don't want this behaviour. Can I disable on sign in even though requireEmailVerification is true? I want to disable access on API level if email not verified, hence why I want the requireEmailVerification true but I dont want to ALWAYS sent an email when unverified tries to sign in. I just really don't like that every time someone tries to sign in an email is beeing sent. Emails aren't cheap for us atm so Id like to limit any possibility for spam attacks (I know rate limitting is an option, but Im also not a fan of beeing able to "sent emails" while the previous token hasnt expired yet)

2025-09-17T13:45:28.129000+00:00
so ``` // (protected)/layout.tsx "use server" import { auth } from "@/lib/auth"; import { headers } from "next/headers"; import { redirect } from "next/navigation"; export default async function ProtectedLayout({ children, }: { children: React.ReactNode; }) { const session = await auth.api.getSession({ headers: await headers(), }); if (!session) { redirect('/auth/sign-in'); } return ( { children } ); } ``` having this at the layout that applies to all my pages that are only accessible for users is the perfect way to do it (+ the optimistic redirects from middleware purely based on getSessionCookie Then if I'd have to use some user info like 7 pages and 3 components deep, im not gonna pass user thru all the components right? FalconiZzare
2025-09-12T10:14:04.376000+00:00
Using it to authorize custom api endpoint access too. ``` import { fromNodeHeaders } from "better-auth/node"; import { auth } from "../auth.js"; export default async function authMiddleware(req, res, next) { try { const session = await auth.api.getSession({ headers: fromNodeHeaders(req.headers) }); if (!session || !session.user) return res.status(401).json({ message: "Authentication required.", success: false }); req.userId = session.session.userId; next(); } catch (err) { console.error(err); res.status(500).json({ message: "Server error!", success: false }); } } ``` for example im using this middleware to make authenticated call to my custom endpoint that needs user info. It can be extended for other use too such as org or teams and stuff. Attaching orgId, userId to the payload during auth saves time and effortc when u perform operation on ur controllers.

In beforeCreateOrganization we update the ctx.body with our new data, but on adapter.createOrganization we still use the old data (...orgData) ```ts const { keepCurrentActiveOrganization: _, userId: __, ...orgData } = ctx.body; if (options?.organizationHooks?.beforeCreateOrganization) { const response = await options?.organizationHooks.beforeCreateOrganization({ organization: orgData, user, }); if (response && typeof response === "object" && "data" in response) { ctx.body = { ...ctx.body, ...response.data, }; } } const organization = await adapter.createOrganization({ organization: { ...orgData, createdAt: new Date(), }, }); ```

FalconiZzare
2025-09-06T16:00:38.257000+00:00
It's the correct behavior. Imagine a scenario.. u logged in to your website a session is created on server,, then for some reason you cleared all data of your browser,, so of course no session token is there,, so you have to login again creating another session,, now you have two sessions on the server and u can use only one cause the previous one, it's gone from client end... There are many other reasons that can cause the scenario and the server has no way of knowing if your user is logging in multiple times intentionally or genuinely. So better to redirect users on the frontend when session is valid so that they cant log in multiple times intentionally by going back.

FalconiZzare
2025-09-06T05:14:55.526000+00:00
I see. If the user can submit the form or click the discord auth button multiple times then with each submission/click a new session is generated. This is because each time it's a new request and server processes it. What you can do to prevent this is redirect the user to another page if a valid session already exists. So when in login page, check authClient.useSession(), if it's not null and has data, that means a valid session is available and no need to login again and redirect the user to another page.
